  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_575143e7-f0cc-4e94-a81f-8f0ffa99e6af'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer11487731188775492633">14-year-old Will Burrows has little in common with his strange, dysfunctional family. In fact, the only bond he shares with his eccentric father is a passion for archaeological excavation. So when his dad mysteriously vanishes, Will is compelled to dig up the truth behind his disappearance. He unearths the unbelievable: a subterranean society that time forgot. "The Colony"</span>
  <span id="freeText11487731188775492633" style="display:none">14-year-old Will Burrows has little in common with his strange, dysfunctional family. In fact, the only bond he shares with his eccentric father is a passion for archaeological excavation. So when his dad mysteriously vanishes, Will is compelled to dig up the truth behind his disappearance. He unearths the unbelievable: a subterranean society that time forgot. "The Colony" has existed unchanged for a century, but it's no benign time capsule of a bygone era. Because the Colony is ruled by a merciless overclass, the Styx. Will must free his father--is he also about to ignite a revolution?</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1558030050" />
    <a title="James Trevino" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52992135-james-trevino"><img alt="James Trevino" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559580766p2/52992135.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1558030050?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Trevino" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Trevino" href="/user/show/52992135-james-trevino">James Trevino</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1558030050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3782437931404477910">This is the beginning of one of my favorite series of all time, but for some reason I never wrote a review for it. And I decided I really should because more people need to know about it.<br/>I first heard of Tunnels in a newspaper (yes, really that long ago!) where it was deemed the 'The next Harry Potter' (and God knows we had a lot of those). Needless to say, they are nothing alike, except for the fact that they were discovered by the same editor. <br/>Tunnels tells the story of Will Burrows, a boy wit</span>
  <span id="freeText3782437931404477910" style="display:none">This is the beginning of one of my favorite series of all time, but for some reason I never wrote a review for it. And I decided I really should because more people need to know about it.<br />I first heard of Tunnels in a newspaper (yes, really that long ago!) where it was deemed the 'The next Harry Potter' (and God knows we had a lot of those). Needless to say, they are nothing alike, except for the fact that they were discovered by the same editor. <br />Tunnels tells the story of Will Burrows, a boy with a passion for digging. That is what leads him to the discovery of an underground world under London and to a bunch of adventures. As a genre, I would say Tunnels is an adventure book by excellence. It reminded me a lot of Jules Verne's works, with a twist. A very dark twist. Tunnels is recommended for children apparently, but I think it is at the very least YA. It is violent and quite scary at times (and I am a Stephen King and John Saul reader so I should know). <br />And if we accept that it is YA, don't think that you know what it's like. I feel like the YA genre is plagued lately by awfully written love stories and love triangles. That is not the case here. Tunnels is edge of your seat suspenseful, gorgeously written and the ending is one of the biggest mind-f**cks I've ever seen (seriously, WTF??).<br />It is also the kind of book that I could recommend to everyone, no matter what age. <br />So yeah, please do yourself a favor and read it. JAMES OUT.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3782437931404477910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_20336428" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20336428" />
    <a title="Jaclyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/353795-jaclyn"><img alt="Jaclyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522318308p2/353795.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/20336428?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaclyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaclyn" href="/user/show/353795-jaclyn">Jaclyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who like dirt and avoid showers</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20336428" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6006257563190280323">Meh. This wasn't my kind of book at all. I was one of the multitudes who got sucked into the "next Harry Potter" hype and the one thing I've learned from the experience is that there isn't going to be a next Harry Potter, so I should just get over it.<br/><br/>Now, to the book. It's the story of Will Burrows, a Londoner whose great passion is conducting archaeological digs with his dad. When his dad goes missing, Will enlists the help of his friend Chester. Together they stumble on an entire underground c</span>
  <span id="freeText6006257563190280323" style="display:none">Meh. This wasn't my kind of book at all. I was one of the multitudes who got sucked into the "next Harry Potter" hype and the one thing I've learned from the experience is that there isn't going to be a next Harry Potter, so I should just get over it.<br /><br />Now, to the book. It's the story of Will Burrows, a Londoner whose great passion is conducting archaeological digs with his dad. When his dad goes missing, Will enlists the help of his friend Chester. Together they stumble on an entire underground civilization that exists in secrecy, miles below London. Sounds fantastic, right? GREAT story concept. The problem is, the book is missing several elements that, had it had them, would have made it a much better story and much worthier of "next Harry Potter" hype. First of all, the main difference I can see is that this isn't a story of good vs. evil. It's a story of moral ambivalence vs. evil. Yes, there are characters as vile and heinously brutal as Voldemort, but there's no trio, no Dumbledore, no McGonagall, no Sirius or Weasley family to balance them out. You root for Will because there's no one better to root for. (That's to the extent that you care enough to root for anyone.) Along with the lack of a good vs. evil story, there were no lessons to be taken from the book. Now, I don't need everything I read to be a parable or moral fable. But it would have been nice if, at the end of slogging through 464 pages of bleak, grim, dark and mucky ambiguity, you had something to show for it. You don't. There's no payoff, nothing to make you feel that the book was a worthwhile experience. Yes, I know it's a series, and I didn't expect a nice tight ending. But the Harry Potter books, while setting the stage for the next installment, all managed to come to a clear resolution and instill a sense of hope. "Tunnels" fails in this regard as well. There's also no humor. Where Harry Potter could be plenty dark in places, there were always light moments, jokes, scenes where Harry actually gets to be happy. NOBODY in the book is ever happy, and I counted a grand total of one joke. And that one joke came about 460 pages into the book, so at that point, I just said "har, har, har" and shook my head. If I wasn't a masochist, I probably wouldn't have finished the book. That said, if you're into dark and dreary, if you can read 464 pages without the slightest break from the dismal, and if you're not expecting the second coming of Potter, you might actually enjoy this. It just wasn't my speed.<br /><br />As to whether I'll read the next one when it comes out, I'm undecided. I'll probably wait and see how I feel, but I know one thing: I'll take it out of the library. I'm not wasting another dollar on this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6006257563190280323" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer15018547171267927267">I don't remember who recommended this book to me, but I didn't really like it. It took sooooooooooooooooooooooooooooooooo long for the author to say anything. The action took so long to develop and when there finally was action, there was too much dialogue and unnecessary description that it took the reader out of the action. I was just groping my through it the whole time waiting for things to happen. I think the book had potential, but the writing was so bad I just went crazy. It's like it was</span>
  <span id="freeText15018547171267927267" style="display:none">I don't remember who recommended this book to me, but I didn't really like it. It took sooooooooooooooooooooooooooooooooo long for the author to say anything. The action took so long to develop and when there finally was action, there was too much dialogue and unnecessary description that it took the reader out of the action. I was just groping my through it the whole time waiting for things to happen. I think the book had potential, but the writing was so bad I just went crazy. It's like it was void of emotion--of any kind. And for supposedly taking place in London or England, it sounded too American.</span>

I noticed that the book noted editor, who found Harry Potter, but it is the only link with Harry. It is a story about a boy Will Burrows and his father Roger who are mystified researchers history. His father was a curator at the museum, and with his son secretly engaged excavated and exploring the underground tunnels of London. Will is the skinny boy of fourteen years, has completely white hair and his skin is ve</span>
  <span id="freeText9671945246314411635" style="display:none">The book "Tunnels" I found on a shelf in a public library, I read a little summary. I noticed that the book noted editor, who found Harry Potter, but it is the only link with Harry. It is a story about a boy Will Burrows and his father Roger who are mystified researchers history. His father was a curator at the museum, and with his son secretly engaged excavated and exploring the underground tunnels of London. Will is the skinny boy of fourteen years, has completely white hair and his skin is very sensitive to sunlight. For this reason, it is often the target of school hooligans, but there he meets his friend Chester with whom he becomes friends. Honestly Will family is completely dysfunctional, father is fully engaged in the research, a mother constantly lying in bed, and his younger sister Rebecca keeps the entire house on their feet making sure that her family is not hungry and clean. Wills father of an old man who frequently visits the museum receives a unique object and he begins to investigate its origin. Soon afterward his father disappears. Will with his friend Chester trying to find out where his father disappeared. This research will take them deep below the surface of London in a world that is not even a little bit in favor of people from the earth's surface. Frankly, a story written by Roderick Gordon and Brian Williams is dark, full of danger, hidden secrets, and lies. Everything was Will world will fade away like soap bubbles. This is a dark fantasy book do not expect the world of Harry Potter, the world in which to find Will and his friend, not even a little bit of hospitality, it is deadly and sinister. The dangers are real and ruthless enemies is real. I would recommend the book to all lovers of fantasy books, and I hope to continue to read because the story has just begun.</span>

  <span id="freeText9328508796849032031" style="display:none">Well, this is the last YA (type) book I'm planning to read in the foreseeable future, and I'm just as glad. I've read several lately that have disappointed me. This had also.<br /><br />I found the book mildly interesting as it opened with the "supposed" father son digging team stocking the little museum and saving their own prizes. But the book takes a turn and becomes something totally different. This (of course) isn't necessarily a bad thing, it could have been a very good thing. But if a book uses this ploy, what it changes into needs to be, "good". I didn't find this so.<br /><br />This book was a strange combination. It sort of lost my interest yet still annoyed me. I'd like to see the reaction of some of the people who were so "down" on Harry Potter (Books by the way I like greatly) to this tome of depressing betrayal, fouled up parentage, poor friends, disintegrating families and violent hate filled mobs. I'd like their comparison between any negative scenes they may have seen in Rowling to the dual to the death with machetes we get here. <br /><br />I don't plan to follow this up with anything else from the author. I got through to the end, it is readable and I'm sure some will like it greatly, I'm not one of them. </span>

  <span id="freeText5234655827411336204" style="display:none">Reviewed by Joan Stradling for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />Like his father, fourteen-year-old Will Burrows has an obsession with archaeological digs. <br /><br />When his father disappears, Will is determined to find him. With the help of his best friend, Chester, Will discovers a network of tunnels under modern-day London.     <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1312086051?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dhen Dhen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dhen Dhen" href="/user/show/43913649-dhen-dhen">Dhen Dhen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43913649-dhen-dhen?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1312086051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12970547405383875473">Okay, first of all, I didn't expect this one to be really good. I just saw it in my shelf (God knows when I bought it!) and decided to read it to past the time, nothing much. <br/><br/>But oh my, I was so wrong. I was prepared to give it a 1star after reading 3-4 chapters. Because the idea of 2 teenage boys obssessed with digging tunnels doesn't appeal to me. I already predicted that they'll discover something from ancient history down there. They did. BUT IT WAS TOTALLY BETTER THAN I EXPECTED. Yep, that'</span>
  <span id="freeText12970547405383875473" style="display:none">Okay, first of all, I didn't expect this one to be really good. I just saw it in my shelf (God knows when I bought it!) and decided to read it to past the time, nothing much. <br /><br />But oh my, I was so wrong. I was prepared to give it a 1star after reading 3-4 chapters. Because the idea of 2 teenage boys obssessed with digging tunnels doesn't appeal to me. I already predicted that they'll discover something from ancient history down there. They did. BUT IT WAS TOTALLY BETTER THAN I EXPECTED. Yep, that's how I feel about it. To think it has 5 more books following it! I better fetch some copies now.<br /><br />I understand why some people keep calling it "the next Harry Potter" because of the similarity of the wizarding world with the colony, and the muggles and topsoilers. But please stop. There ain't gonna be a next Harry Potter. End of story. <br /><br />There was a part in the book where I really needed to put it down: Chester's failed attempt to escaped. I almost cried. His chapters always want me to go and save him. He's my favorite character next to Caleb. I think they're the reason why the story moved for Will.<br /><br />A lot more questions were left unanswered. I don't know how fate would save Will, he's totally stucked. Can't go to Topsoil, can't go to Colony, where to next? Where would you go if the only two worlds that exist you wants you dead? I'm so excited to read the other books!<br /><br />Watch out for Rebecca. Keep your bitch radar alert at all times.</span>

<div id="review_38537699" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38537699" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/650953-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1198024083p2/650953.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38537699?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/650953-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/650953-jennifer?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/650953-jennifer?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38537699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer829053385500056649">In a nutshell, this is my review (actually the "conclusion" of the review put here so that people don't have to read my babble if they don't want to):<br/><br/>While the plot of <i>Tunnels</i> may have been a little skimpy or slow, it offers so much possibility and food for thought and the imagination, especially in its unique and mysterious subterranean setting and moral ambiguity, that I can't help but give it a positive review. (I will admit that the book may deserve three stars rather than four, and that see</span>
  <span id="freeText829053385500056649" style="display:none">In a nutshell, this is my review (actually the "conclusion" of the review put here so that people don't have to read my babble if they don't want to):<br /><br />While the plot of <i>Tunnels</i> may have been a little skimpy or slow, it offers so much possibility and food for thought and the imagination, especially in its unique and mysterious subterranean setting and moral ambiguity, that I can't help but give it a positive review. (I will admit that the book may deserve three stars rather than four, and that seeing one-star reviews of the book may have swayed my decision). In the end, the sequel, <i>Deeper</i> will tell if the potential of <i>Tunnels</i> is fulfilled. <br /><br />Perhaps I enjoyed this book more than others because I didn't start reading it with the hope/expectation that it would be the "next Harry Potter." On the contrary, although I have enjoyed children and young adult fantasy since I was actually a child, long before all the hype of the Harry Potter novels, I approach all new novels of the genre with some skepticism, because, not only do I feel that I have read all of the great children's fantasy fiction (or at least remember them with such childhood fondness that I don't feel that anything can top them), but worse, I feel like the market is being flooded with mediocre children's fantasy novels in an attempt to cash in on that exact sentiment, that people are yearning to find the "next Harry Potter."<br /><br />That said, I can understand why many say that <i>Tunnels</i> gets off to a slow start and doesn't have as much "action" as they would like. It seems to take about a little less than a third of the novel for any of the "real" action to begin, and doesn't contain as many mini-adventures as the Harry Potter novels. However, I personally think that this portion of the novel was well spent in establishing and developing the characters. Furthermore, I think that the strength of <i>Tunnels</i> comes from the character development, moral ambiguity, and descriptions of the <i>Tunnels</i>' underground city, the very descriptions the many insist make the novel "slow," or "boring." <br /><br />Although, I like many others, was wondering when Will would finally explore the underground city promised by the book jacket, I think that the description of Will and his Topsoil family was well worth the number of pages, because it gave Will a three-dimensional quality and alerted the reader to the fact that the characters and families in the story were supposed to be complex, with individuals that weren't wholly good or evil, and families that couldn't be easily categorized as perfect or dysfunctional. Developing Will's Topsoil family in the way that they did, the author's also laid the groundwork for subtly addressing issues of family loyalty, and the yearning to belong.<br /><br />As I mentioned earlier, I think the the relative (as compared to stories like <i>Harry Potter</i> and <i>The Chronicles of Narnia</i> ) moral ambiguity of <i>Tunnels</i> is one of its strengths rather than a weakness. Although we all enjoy tales of good triumphing over evil and everyone (except the villains, of course) living happily ever after, what sets <i>Tunnels</i> apart from much other mediocre children's fantasy currently flying off bookstore shelves right now is the fact that the issues are more complex. Although the Styx, the mysterious and ruthless ruling class of the underworld embody, and are even called "evil" more than once in the text, is this really the case? What made them the way that they are? Why are they privileged to torture the way that they do? Even if we can easily label the Styx as evil, what about the other Colonists living underground? Are they evil merely because they take the ruthlessness of the Styx for granted? Are all Colonists as evil as Will's initial experience with the subterranean dwellers lead the reader to believe? There are these questions and more, because neither the Topsoilers nor the subterranean Colonists are portrayed as "good" or "bad." While the Colonists live under the rule of the cruel Styx seemingly bound to the indoctrination of the church, they are right in their accusations that the Topsoilers ruin and pollute the earth. In short, all the characters in <i>Tunnels</i> are portrayed as humans with all their faults and strengths, whether or not they reside above- or below-ground, which allows the novel to touch upon and play with interesting ideas about human nature, the motivations of humans, both individuals and mobs, and the ultimate effects on society.<br /><br />As for the third thing that I could forsee people complaining about slowing up the pace of the novel is the description of the underground world. Once again, I think that this is actually a strength, because the setting conceived by Gordon and Williams is refreshingly different than other children's fantasy novels. From the authors' descriptions, I, personally imagined and amazing world that I hadn't previously seen anywhere, not even in my imagination. The descriptions also help to convey Will and Dr. Burrow's fascination and with the world around them, which is something that the authors' hope to communicate through their writing. What makes <i>Tunnels</i> subterranean world unique and more captivating than that in novels such as <i>The City of Ember</i> and <i>Myst: the Book of D'Ni</i> is the mysterious history of it. The novel makes us wonder not only about the founding of the Colony by a man who was supposed to have died in a fire, but also about the pre-Colonial civilizations that built the Eternal City and why.<br /><br />As with the moral ambiguity of the "sides" in <i>Tunnels</i>, the underground setting of the novel, and the mystery behind the subterranean land's history hook the reader. While the plot of <i>Tunnels</i> may have been a little skimpy, it offers so much possibility and food for thought and the imagination, that I can't help but give it a positive review. (I will admit that the book may deserve three stars rather than four, and that seeing one-star reviews of the book may have swayed my decision). I suppose that the sequel, <i>Deeper</i> will tell if the potential of <i>Tunnels</i> is fulfilled. </span>
  <a data-text-id="829053385500056649" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_47144810" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/47144810" />
    <a title="Sandy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1812229-sandy"><img alt="Sandy" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/47144810?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy" href="/user/show/1812229-sandy">Sandy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer47144810&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer47144810" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7539776675247276047">Fun, Adventurous and Creepy. Ignore the "next Harry Potter" hype. No book is going to be the next Harry Potter but many can be nearly as fun and worth the read and this book is one of those.<br/>I cared about the characters and what happened to them and couldn't wait to find out what came next. It was surprisingly creepy and there are even some fairly gross images; some from bloody fighting, some from disgusting food. The plot didn't go where I expected it to; I thought Will and his father would find</span>
  <span id="freeText7539776675247276047" style="display:none">Fun, Adventurous and Creepy. Ignore the "next Harry Potter" hype. No book is going to be the next Harry Potter but many can be nearly as fun and worth the read and this book is one of those.<br />I cared about the characters and what happened to them and couldn't wait to find out what came next. It was surprisingly creepy and there are even some fairly gross images; some from bloody fighting, some from disgusting food. The plot didn't go where I expected it to; I thought Will and his father would find their way down to an underground town where the inhabitants were unfriendly and chased them. I didn't expect the scary and evil Styx and the cult like society they preside over. Or that the Styx and their henchmen would go "topsoil" stalking and kidnapping anyone who accidently discovered even the smallest trace of the underground dwellers. Those added elements were what gave the book an extra creepy vibe. I wouldn't recommend this book for younger readers who might be easily scared. If your child enjoys a little thrill though you can easily read this book with them and you'll likely enjoy it just as much as they do.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7539776675247276047" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer48114788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7674439120346373335"> It's not that this book isn't well-written, that part works fine. It's just the story! When I finished it, I was speechless. It had gone from bad to worse and then just ended. The happy resolution never happened. The goal of our little hero was never achieved. The book ended with a murder. I was left feeling dismal and cheated.<br/> And this is a children's book! I picked it up for my kids and previewed it because the cover is so grabbing - the light and the title seem to shine out of the cover, but</span>
  <span id="freeText7674439120346373335" style="display:none"> It's not that this book isn't well-written, that part works fine. It's just the story! When I finished it, I was speechless. It had gone from bad to worse and then just ended. The happy resolution never happened. The goal of our little hero was never achieved. The book ended with a murder. I was left feeling dismal and cheated.<br /> And this is a children's book! I picked it up for my kids and previewed it because the cover is so grabbing - the light and the title seem to shine out of the cover, but I haven't recommended it to any of them.<br /> Adam, my most voracious reader at 16, read it anyway and was as appalled as I was. And this is the worst part: I had an opportunity to buy the newly released sequel at half off and so I did (the cover pulls one in) in the hope that all would come to a happy resolution. I haven't read it yet, but Adam got half-way through and quit. The second book is called Deeper in case anyone wants to know what to avoid.</span>

                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer81747082&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81747082" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17911690280314345643">Review by: Dorien Williams 206-12<br/><br/><br/>1.	What did you think the book was about?<br/>		<br/><br/>The book was about a boy named Will who's father is an archaeologist. He and his dad love to dig together, until his dad mysteriously disappears. With the help of his friend Chester, Will starts looking for his dad. While the two of them where digging (they thought that there may have been a cave in while Will's dad was in one of the tunnels) they come across a secret underground civilization. After a bit of trouble Will</span>
  <span id="freeText17911690280314345643" style="display:none">Review by: Dorien Williams 206-12<br /><br /><br />1.	What did you think the book was about?<br />		<br /><br />The book was about a boy named Will who's father is an archaeologist. He and his dad love to dig together, until his dad mysteriously disappears. With the help of his friend Chester, Will starts looking for his dad. While the two of them where digging (they thought that there may have been a cave in while Will's dad was in one of the tunnels) they come across a secret underground civilization. After a bit of trouble Will finds out that his dad just past through about a week before. And that he's gone into the Deeps, a dark place closer to the center of the earth where horrible creatures and contraptions are beyond imagination. While on the run from the Styx (a secret cult that everyone in the Colony fears) Will and some companions head into the Deeps to find Will's father.<br /><br /><br />4. How did the book compare to other books by the author (or other books in the same genre)?<br />		<br />Compared to all the other fiction books i've read "Tunnels" is definitely one of the best. With a surprise around every corner. And chase scenes like when Will was running from the mysterious man with extremely pale skin and dressed completely in black. <br />		<br /><br />5.	 What about the plot? Did it pull you in; or did you feel you had to force yourself to read the book?<br />	<br />The plot of the book was pretty good, but the beginning was very boring just talking about the characters descriptions which really didn't improved the book at all. But later on the plot started thickening as Will went deeper into the newly discovered world and it was hard to put the book down.<br /><br /><br />6. Were the characters realistic? Would you want to meet any of the characters? Did you like them? Hate them?<br /><br />All the main characters were realistic, they didn't have super powers or anything like that. They had regular jobs. I would like to meet Mr.Burrows (Will's dad) because while I was reading the book I was wondering what was going through his mind when he was going deeper underground. Was he scared, curious, etc? I liked all the characters except Will's mom because all she did the whole book was watch TV in the living room. I felt she was really just dead wait in the story and that the authors might as well of marked her dead.<br /><br /><br />7. Did the actions of the characters seem plausible? Why? Why not?<br /><br /> The actions seemed plausible except the fact that the Colony (the name of the underground civilization) could survive underground for so long with no real sun light. And of course with no sun light there would be no vegetables or fruit and these are vital for surviving. But otherwise everything seemed plausible. None of the main characters had anything more than being really (but humanly) strong. Like Mr.Jerome and uncle Tam.<br /><br /><br />8. If one (or more) of the characters made a choice that had moral implications, would you have made the same decision? Why? Why not?<br /><br />When Chester agreed to help Will find his father I thought that was a morel decision. Because he didn't have to help Will especially when he knows how dangerous digging that deep can be. And I would have to say that I would make the same choice because I could never just stand back and not help someone help their dad especially if he was in peril.<br /><br /><br />9. How would the book have been different if it had taken place in a different time or place?<br /><br />Nothing in the book would drastically change if it took place in a different place in the world. Or if it took place in a different time like the 1800's. I don't think it would take them any longer to get on Mr.Burrows's trail but in the future the technology would probably be more advanced so that would speed up the process. Because they didn't use any electronics besides flashlights for a bit. And the only real piece of machinery was a train but besides that they just used shovels for digging.<br /><br /><br />11. How are the book's images symbolically significant? Do the images help to develop the plot, or help to define characters?<br /><br />The book's images weren't very important and didn't help the book out a lot. Like when it was describing what Chester looks like, with "pale skin, freckles and orange hair". I don't think that improved the plot at all, because even if he looked completely different nothing would change in the plot of the story.<br /><br /><br />12. Did the book end the way you expected?<br /><br />The book didn't end anything like I expected. I thought for sure they'd find Mr.Burrows and not have gotten on a train "accelerating into the very heart of the earth". Because to me that doesn't sound like a very happy ending especially when "the deeper you go the bigger the dangers". But the ending did leave room for a sequel, because the readers would want to find out what's waiting for them in the "heart of the earth".<br /><br /><br />13. Would you recommend this book to other readers? To your close friend?<br /><br /> I would definitely recommend this book to other readers who enjoy fiction books. Because the underground civilization is possible but no one would invest the time, risk or money to making it possible. Nor could the people in the Colony survive without vegetation.<br /><br /><br />14. If you were casting these characters in a movie- what actors/actresses would play them?<br /><br /> If I was going to make a movie about this book I'd choose mainly british actors because the book takes place in britain, so it'd be easier for the actors to speak (not having to change accents). A few examples are that; Daniel Radcliff would play Will because he fits the description and does well as the main character in movies. Rupert Grant would play Chester because he also fits the description and he does well as the "sidekick" in films. Another is Jason Statham would play Mr.Jerome because he looks muscular and is quiet like the character.<br /><br /><br />15. What was your favorite part/scene of the book?<br /><br />My favorite part of the book was when I found out what they ate down in the Colony. They couldn't eat vegetables with no sun light and you need vegetables to survive and the smell of too many animals would be overwhelming. Thats why I was surprised when I found out that they ate rat jerky and some kind of maggot/grub when Cal, Mr.Jerome and Will sat down for supper and Will "watched in horror as Cal bit down on one of the squirming white creatures".<br /><br /><br />17. Did you learn anything from the book that you didn't already know?<br /><br />I wasn't really expecting to learn anything new or educational from the book and I didn't. I think the main reason is because it's a fiction book so most of the things in it aren't a reality. Like a human society who can survive without vegetables or fruit is impossible. And an underground civilization is technically possible but still doesn't exist. <br /><br /><br />18. Everyone- On a scale from 1-5 what would you give this book- what would have made this book better?<br /><br /> I give the book a 4 out of 5. It would have been better if Rebecca (Will's sister) had done more in the book. For example instead of staying home and looking after the mom the whole story, she could have surprised the readers in someway. By knowing more about everything that was going on, or something like that. Something to make it harder for the reader to put the book down.<br /><br /><br /><br />19. Were there any personality traits in the character that you could identify with?<br /><br />I guess I can relate to Will's curiosity because he's always asking questions like "How does this orb thingy work?" or "Who are your founding fathers?". And I'm always asking questions too. I can relate to Rebecca too because of her extra steps in security, like when she saw someone going through their garbage and said to herself "good luck finding anything in there ,I burned all the bills and credit card invoices.". Because I always tell my mom to burn or at least shred the stuff that people can use to steal her identity.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17911690280314345643" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5826619385265933255">I don't remember why I chose this book, but I didn't really like it. It took so long for the author to say anything.   <span id="freeText5826619385265933255" style="display:none">I don't remember why I chose this book, but I didn't really like it. It took so long for the author to say anything. The action took so long to develop and when there finally was action, there was too much dialogue and unnecessary description that it took the reader out of the action. I was choking myself through it the whole time waiting for things to happen. The book I read was Tunnels by Roderick Gordon. Its about fouteen- year old Will Burrows lives with his family in London. He has little in common with them except for a passion for digging which he shares with his father.When his father suddenly disappears down an unknown tunnel that they've been exploring for a month. Will decides to investigate with his friend Chester from school. Soon they find themselves deep underground, where they unearth a deep and dark secret. A secret that could endanger their lives. <br />hink the book had potential. The storyline was really creative but, they didn't invest enough time into their characters.The writing was so bad I just went crazy and for supposedly taking place in London or England, it sounded too American because of how they put their text together because instead of using english words they used american words like a house there would be called a flat. Instead they just called it a house. <br /><br />There is a sequel to this book which I will not read. This is a series but the first book was just so bad that i'm going to put a rest to the author Roderick Gordon. This is not a book I recommend for anyone unless you like slow action books that takes forever to get to the idea. <br /></span>

<div id="review_83991209" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83991209" />
    <a title="Dick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1975365-dick"><img alt="Dick" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/83991209?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dick" href="/user/show/1975365-dick">Dick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83991209" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16918051458638487049"> Like City of Ember this is another underground dystopia story. The main character is Will Burroughs, a young adolescent boy who lives in London with his a dysfunctional family: an aloof, absent-minded archeologist father, a distant depressed mother, and a hostile older teenage sister. Will takes after his father with a keen interest in excavation. He helps with his father's "digs" and conducts his own assisted by his friend Chester. The father is the curator of a local museum which gives him ac</span>
  <span id="freeText16918051458638487049" style="display:none"> Like City of Ember this is another underground dystopia story. The main character is Will Burroughs, a young adolescent boy who lives in London with his a dysfunctional family: an aloof, absent-minded archeologist father, a distant depressed mother, and a hostile older teenage sister. Will takes after his father with a keen interest in excavation. He helps with his father's "digs" and conducts his own assisted by his friend Chester. The father is the curator of a local museum which gives him access to maps of old tunnel systems of the London Underground system and by digging into the old tunnels Will and his father discover and are taken prisoner by a whole underworld living below London. The underworld is called The Colony and it's an authoritarian dystopia that's as familiar as any that's ruled human history on the surface of the earth. The rationale for it's continued existence is not particularly well explained, and I found the story somewhat tedious. To add to my dissatisfaction the story doesn't resolve, but ends with Will, his father, and friend Chester escaping into the empty tunnels below the colony requiring a sequel to resolve this big bugger. This is definitely for the die-hard fantasy reading middle school boy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16918051458638487049" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780439871778" href="/book/show/1338404.Tunnels">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5881438-ellen?shelf=never-finished">never-finished</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer189690079" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18071708727717253737">Despite a recommendation from a friend that this new series was reminiscent of C.S. Lewis' Magician's Nephew, this book was a huge disappointment. True there is an obsessed, uncaring relative of a boy who stumbles on to another world, but the similarities end there. Tunnels is the story of a family who is distracted, at best, and dysfunctional at worst. The father locks himself in the basement to get away from his family; the mother cares for nothing except her TV; and the sister is obsessed wit</span>
  <span id="freeText18071708727717253737" style="display:none">Despite a recommendation from a friend that this new series was reminiscent of C.S. Lewis' Magician's Nephew, this book was a huge disappointment. True there is an obsessed, uncaring relative of a boy who stumbles on to another world, but the similarities end there. Tunnels is the story of a family who is distracted, at best, and dysfunctional at worst. The father locks himself in the basement to get away from his family; the mother cares for nothing except her TV; and the sister is obsessed with cleaning and shoulders the whole burden of running the family. Will is a youngster with a passion for excavations and uncovering treasures. I could admire him for being a bit of a misfit and discovering the hidden world, but the problem was, the other world was no better than the world he left. There was no hope, nothing positive anywhere. The world underground is controlling, dark, and negative in every way. The last straw for me was when the entire community was forced to attend church where the evil Styx preacher, complete with a iron cross and rivets in the background, completely twists and misquotes Scripture. Seven hours into the audiobook, I shut it off and deleted. Very disappointing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18071708727717253737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_488030014" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/488030014" />
    <a title="Kathleen Fowler" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3560723-kathleen-fowler"><img alt="Kathleen Fowler" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1288949581p2/3560723.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/488030014?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen Fowler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen Fowler" href="/user/show/3560723-kathleen-fowler">Kathleen Fowler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer488030014" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18355498832765547359">The premise of this book is interesting and it’s nicely illustrated with creepy ink drawings. Alas, it’s far too long for what it has to offer, and quite poorly written. I was put off by the way adult characters were consistently portrayed as cold, self-absorbed, and extremely flawed. There were only two adults in the entire story who were decent. Also, for those parents who might wish to know, the book abounds with smoking, drunken brawling, and kids drinking and mocking their religion. I didn’</span>
  <span id="freeText18355498832765547359" style="display:none">The premise of this book is interesting and it’s nicely illustrated with creepy ink drawings. Alas, it’s far too long for what it has to offer, and quite poorly written. I was put off by the way adult characters were consistently portrayed as cold, self-absorbed, and extremely flawed. There were only two adults in the entire story who were decent. Also, for those parents who might wish to know, the book abounds with smoking, drunken brawling, and kids drinking and mocking their religion. I didn’t blame them, mind you--it was a more than usually silly religion; but as I said, some parents might wish to be forewarned.<br /><br />What offended me most was the sloppiness of the writing. There was a sandstorm that “threatened to knock him off his feet,” but afterward this character successfully located the “little pile of organic matter” he had gathered to start a fire with. There was also a cat who investigated something briefly before “lifting a leg over it.” There’s a first. These are just two examples out of many.<br /><br />The authors used a lot of strange words. I couldn’t figure out if they were being creative or were simply careless. And what did they mean when they wrote things like a man “swore blindly as he stumbled?”<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18355498832765547359" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4286116571343437809">A bit slow, and perhaps not needed - tunnels is the start to a series of 6 books that wasn't what I was expecting. Having put this down as a top middle grade/lower YA novel some of the stuff that this book deals with is quite a bit older and so would recommend for those aged 15+<br/><br/>In terms of story, this felt completely unnecessary and seemed to be a starting point rather than an actual full fledged story, with situations being discovered and then just never mentioned again (may be mentioned in lat</span>
  <span id="freeText4286116571343437809" style="display:none">A bit slow, and perhaps not needed - tunnels is the start to a series of 6 books that wasn't what I was expecting. Having put this down as a top middle grade/lower YA novel some of the stuff that this book deals with is quite a bit older and so would recommend for those aged 15+<br /><br />In terms of story, this felt completely unnecessary and seemed to be a starting point rather than an actual full fledged story, with situations being discovered and then just never mentioned again (may be mentioned in later instalments but I highly doubt it) and a completely out of the blue section which was completely redundant three pages later.<br /><br />That being said, the last few chapters were exemplary - I really enjoyed them and wished that perhaps the story should have had a little less filler and more of the action sequences and character development of the last chapters. I also was impressed by the twist in this story - although not completely surprised I do think it was interesting and well thought out.<br /><br />I think I am invested enough to at least try the sequels, but overall this book was a disappointment</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mmyOUKoOGriQH7+enTt6SMU/H1a0XtObllQdiyIDNuQy05ujb7c/yJvj39FBehuVtlfasWrudJspeXLLoHgHQQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kXvq3AuB+IwblttWmppKDzyMz2HUd0yurQ/DoJJbwIw5xP8vzjjd/BBquxlG2yvST+QKhgrH664SIqzgECDxKQ==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/573850.Roderick_Gordon">About Roderick Gordon</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1031332186832086763">Roderick Gordon is the author of the Tunnels series of books. Born in 1960, he grew up in Highgate, North London, and eventually went to University College where he dabbled in genetics and listened to Joy Division. After graduating without the faintest idea what he wanted to do for the rest of his life, he spent some time in the wilderness when he played in a few bands, then somehow fell into a jo</span>
  <span id="freeText1031332186832086763" style="display:none">Roderick Gordon is the author of the Tunnels series of books. Born in 1960, he grew up in Highgate, North London, and eventually went to University College where he dabbled in genetics and listened to Joy Division. After graduating without the faintest idea what he wanted to do for the rest of his life, he spent some time in the wilderness when he played in a few bands, then somehow fell into a job doing corporate finance for an investment bank in the City of London. He genuinely thought this was all that the future held for him until he was made redundant in 2001.<br />But Roderick surprised himself by working on a book with help from an old university friend and, in 2005, he self-published it as The Highfield Mole, which caught the attention of Barry Cunningham, founder of Chicken House, a publisher of children’s books. Following a period of editing, Barry republished it as Tunnels in July 2007. After intense media interest around its launch, Tunnels was published in almost forty countries and was a New York Times Bestseller, achieving sales of more than a million copies worldwide. Shortly after publication the film rights were purchased by US-based Relativity Media, and Mikael Håfström has been appointed as director. Roderick followed Tunnels with further books in the series, Deeper, Freefall, Closer, Spiral and, finally, Terminal in 2013.<br /><br />He has just released a new book called Summerhouse Land in a very limited run of hardbacks. Please see <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.summerhouseland.com">www.summerhouseland.com</a> for more details.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1031332186832086763" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
